				<h4 id="NUR273" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NUR 273 &nbsp; Nursing of Adults and Children III Clinical (0)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 240, BIO 243, CHM 101, CHM 103, ENG 101, NUR 103, NUR 113, NUR 123, BIO 241, BIO 244, NUR 104, NUR 114, NUR 124, PSY 101, BIO 245, BIO 247.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NUR 253, NUR 263.</p>
								
				<p>Students plan, administer, and care for patients in labor and delivery, postpartum, and nursery units as well as in medical and surgical units in area hospital/health care facilities. Twelve clinical laboratory hours per week.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

				<h4 id="NUR274" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NUR 274 &nbsp; Nursing of Adults and Children IV Clinical (0)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 240, BIO 243, CHM 101, CHM 103,  NUR 103, NUR 113, NUR 123, BIO 241, BIO 244, BIO 245, BIO 247, PSY 101, NUR 104, NUR 114, NUR 124, NUR 253, NUR 263, NUR 273, SOC 101, ENG 101,  ENG 102 or any LIT</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NUR 254, NUR 264.</p>
								
				<p>Gaining independence, students plan, administer, and evaluate total nursing care to patients and begin supervising others giving care. Emphasis is placed upon the nurse and patient functioning in a homeostatic milieu, with consideration of physical, psychosocial, ethnocultural and spiritual aspects of development. A 5-week preceptorship provides transition between student and practitioner. Sixteen clinical laboratory hours per week.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

																											</p>
			</div>
				
					<h3>Occupational Therapy</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="OTA100" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 100 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Occupational Therapy Assistant I (4)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 270 (taken previously or concurrently) BIO 250A/B(BIO 240/243), ENG 101</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> BIO 270 (taken previously or concurrently), OTA 103</p>
								
				<p>Acceptance in the OTA Program. Introduction to occupational therapy, including its history, philosophy, and practice base in relation to treatment in psychosocial dysfunction, physical disabilities, and developmental pediatrics. Theories guiding occupational therapy practice, values and ethics of the profession. Exploration of oral and written communication skills. Overview of occupational therapy process and the OTA role in screening, assessment, treatment planning, treatment implementation, and discharge. Examination of role of occupational therapy personnel in variety of treatment settings, including concepts related to client-practitioner interaction and communication and the importance of collaboration with clients, caregivers, and other health care professionals. Level I Fieldwork opportunities to apply basic occupational therapy principles and techniques and observe roles of OTs and other allied health professionals. Four lecture hours and three hours per week. Level I fieldwork beginning week six for six weeks.&nbsp;<em>Fall</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="OTA102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 102 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Occupational Therapy Assistant II (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 100</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 112, OTA 104/114, OTA 207/217</p>
								
				<p>Introduction of beginning skills in occupational therapy treatment in psychosocial dysfunction. Major theories guiding occupational therapy practice in psychosocial treatment and their application to sensory motor, psychosocial, and cognitive development through the life span. Emphasis on group leadership and facilitation, development of communication and observation skills, and use of self as a therapeutic modality. Examination of issues related to death and dying. Exploration of occupational therapy process of assessment, treatment planning and treatment implementation and discontinuation of intervention in relation to psychosocial practice issues and concerns. Discussion of concepts of psychosocial intervention with other areas of practice. Role of the OTA in prevention, health maintenance, and quality of life of the individual with psychosocial dysfunction. Three lecture hours.<em>Spring</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="OTA103" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 103 &nbsp; Adaptive Activities I (2)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 270(taken previously or concurrently) BIO 250 A/B (BIO 240/243), ENG 101.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> BIO 270 (taken previously or concurrently), OTA 100.</p>
								
				<p>Acceptance into the OTA program. Use of activities in occupational therapy with primary emphasis on the performance area of play/leisure including, those that address sensory motor, cognitive, and psychosocial performance components. Introduction to common therapeutic media used in OT practice. Introduction to acquisition of basic skills, concepts of activity analysis, instruction of individuals and groups, problem-solving, equipment maintenance, and cost and supply factors. Four lab hours per week. <i>Fall</i></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="OTA104" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 104 &nbsp; Adaptive Activities II (1)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 100</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 102/112, OTA 114, OTA 207/217.</p>
								
				<p>Continuation of use of activities in OT with a primary emphasis on the performance area of work/productive activities that address sensory motor, cognitive, and psychosocial performance components. Activities, strategies, and techniques that emphasize the use of purposeful activities and occupation to enhance role function. Introduction to standardized and non-standardized evaluations using activity based format. Development of more advanced skills that focus on grading and adapting purposeful activities and instructing individuals and groups for therapeutic interventions. One lecture hour per week.&nbsp;<em>Spring</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

				<h4 id="OTA105" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 105 &nbsp; Fundamentals of OTA I (12)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> ENG 101, MAT 098</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 115, OTA 125</p>
								
				<p>Introduction to occupational therapy, including history, philosophy and foundational skills required for OT practice. Context is offered<br />based on the fundamental skills needed in psychosocial dysfunction, physical and cognitive dysfunction, and pediatrics using the<br />Occupational Therapy Practice Framework. Theories guiding OT practice, values, and ethics of the profession discussed.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 105, OTA 115, OTA 125</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 116, OTA 126 MATH Stats for Allied Health</p>
								
				<p>Build on foundation skills needed for OT practice and focuses on fundamental assessment and intervention skills in occupational therapy in<br />psychosocial, physical, cognitive and pediatric dysfunction. Understanding of the OT process of assessment, treatment planning and<br />implementation, transitions and discontinuation of OT services is addressed using the OTPF as a guide.</p>

				<h4 id="OTA115" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 115 &nbsp; Kinesiology/Functional A & P (0)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> ENG 101, MAT 098</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 105, OTA 125</p>
								
				<p>Foundation in the biological, physical, and physiological application in the practice of occupational therapy. Students will demonstrate understanding and knowledge of the structure and function of the human body including the musculoskeletal, nervous, cardiovascular, pulmonary, and endocrine systems. Students will apply knowledge for foundational practice skills such as ROM, assessment of muscle control, transfers, vital signs, body mechanics, client positioning and safe handling techniques.</p>

				<h4 id="OTA203" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 203 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Occupational Therapy III (4)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 102</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 213, OTA 204/214, OTA 209, OTA 218</p>
								
				<p>Occupational therapy process related to physical dysfunction evaluation and treatment procedures including self-care, therapeutic exercise, home management, use of adaptive equipment, work and play-leisure skills. Introduction to remediation in movement difficulties and practiced in the laboratory. Administration of standardized and non-standardized tests and evaluations, and need for demonstrating service competency. Activity analysis, documentation, formulation of goals and objectives, collaboration with occupational therapist on treatment implementation, assessment/ reassessment, and termination of treatment. Level I fieldwork introduces application of occupational therapy procedures under close supervision. Three lecture hours. Three hours Level 1 Fieldwork beginning week four for nine weeks or one week of 30 hours.&nbsp;<em>Fall</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />

				<h4 id="OTA204" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 204 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Occupational Therapy IV (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA-102</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 203/213, OTA 214, OTA 209, OTA 218.</p>
								
				<p>Evaluation and treatment of pediatric population appropriate to role of OTA including development and perceptual motor skills, self-care, design and use of adaptive equipment, and play/leisure issues are explored in relation to normal sensory motor, psychosocial, and cognitive development. Interventions using age appropriate activities. Examination of cultural factors on treatment and treatment implementation, including the importance of collaboration and inclusion of family, care givers, and others in the OT process. Laboratory experiences arranged at on-site daycare center for typically developing and special needs children. Field trip to be arranged. Three lecture hours.&nbsp;<em>Fall</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 100</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 102/112, OTA 104/114, OTA 217</p>
								
				<p>Overview of disease conditions commonly seen for treatment by occupational therapy practitioners. Etiology, symptoms and physical and psychological reactions to these conditions. Basic influences contributing to healthy living. Includes medical terminology and procedures commonly used in occupational therapy.&nbsp;<em>Spring</em></p>

				<h4 id="OTA209" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 209 &nbsp; Health Occupations Seminar (2)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 102</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 203/213, OTA 204/214, OTA 218.</p>
								
				<p>Current trends and issues in the health care system, including legal and ethical components of practice, cultural diversity; OTR-OTA role delineation; supervision; documentation to ensure accountability and reimbursement requirements; community resources; multi-disciplinary approach to treatment; and employability skills. Examination of OTA as director of activity program in relation to assessment, treatment planning, and treatment implementation needs. Issues of continuing professional competency, research and program development, involvement in professional organizations and political advocacy. Exploration of quality assurance and measurement of treatment outcomes as well as credential requirements, compliance with regulations, and the use of non-professional personnel. Two lecture/seminar hours per week.&nbsp;<em>Fall</em></p>

				<h4 id="OTA210" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 210 &nbsp; Occupational Therapy Assistant Practicum I (4)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 203</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 298</p>
								
				<p>Prerequisites: Satisfactory completion of all courses and Level I fieldwork through the fifth semester and GPA of 2.5; free of infectious diseases; current certification in CPR and First Aid; proof of personal accident insurance.</p>
<p>Development of professional skills through supervised application of treatment principles. Fieldwork experience in the treatment of geriatric clients, physically disabled children or adults, or clients with psychosocial dysfunction. Student under direct supervision from an occupational therapy practitioner in all aspects of occupational therapy practice. Requires completion of full time caseload as defined by accreditation standards and the assigned facility. Specific objectives developed by the fieldwork site educator in collaboration with OTA academic fieldwork coordinator. Students are required to complete two full time practicums usually of eight weeks duration.&nbsp;<em>Spring</em></p>

				<h4 id="OTA227" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 227 &nbsp; OTA Practicum II (4)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 205, OTA 215, OTA 225</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 206</p>
								
				<p>Level II Fieldwork is the opportunity to practice in the field under direct supervision of a clinical fieldwork educator. Practice emphasis<br />uses the Occupational Therapy Practice Framework as it relates to documentation, facilitation of activities of daily living performance, ROM/MMT, positioning, splinting, functional activities, functional mobility/transfers, treatment planning and addressing environmental barriers.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="OTA298" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">OTA 298 &nbsp; Occupational Therapy Capstone (1)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> OTA 203</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> OTA 210, OTA 211</p>
								
				<p>Completion of program-culminating experiences for the Occupational Therapy Assistant Associate's degree. Provides an opportunity for application and integration of academic course work into fieldwork experiences. Requires reflection of how the role of occupational therapy and the occupational therapy assistant are demonstrated and delineated in each fieldwork facility. Allows for problem solving approach for adjusting to various work sites and handling feedback from supervisors. Requirements for college standardized testing, state licensure and national certification examination are reviewed. Completes development of professional resume and cover letter for employment.&nbsp;<em>Spring</em></p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
				
					<h3>Philosophy</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PHL101" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHL 101 &nbsp; Introduction to Philosophy (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introduction to philosophical inquiry and historically important philosophical ideas discussed by classical and/or modern philosophers. Topics may include the nature of love, the foundation of ethical action, the nature and limits of knowledge, the essence of truth, and the meaning of technology in contemporary culture.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHL102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHL 102 &nbsp; Introduction to Logic (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Study of techniques and methods for identifying, classifying, clarifying, and evaluating various kinds of reasoning and related uses of language.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PHL160" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHL 160 &nbsp; Ethics (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introductory survey of classical and contemporary theories in field of ethics. Questions considered regarding ideal moral life, nature of good and evil, principles for distinguishing right from wrong, and ethical relativism versus objectivism. Discusses selected moral dilemmas of modern living.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />

					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHL201" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHL 201 &nbsp; World Religion (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introduction to basic doctrines and stories of seven major religions of the world: Hinduism, Buddhism, Confucianism, Taoism, Judaism, Christianity, and Islam.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

				<h4 id="PHL260" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHL 260 &nbsp; Reason and Religion (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> ENG 101</p>
												
				<p>Introduction to Western philosophy of religion. Topics include the character and reliability of religious experience, arguments for and against God?s existence, the meaningfulness of religious language, the problem of evil, and life after death.</p>

				<p>Seminar style course reflecting specializations in fields of philosophy. Titles may include: The Modern and the Postmodern, Democracy and Philosophy, Phenomenology and Existentialism, and Aesthetics.</p>

				<h4 id="PHE102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHE 102 &nbsp; Concepts:  Drugs (2)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Organized to provide a measure of sequential development and interrelatedness of subjects pertaining to psychoactive drugs and drug-taking behaviors. Sections include overview of drug problems in America, examination of effects of various drugs such as alcohol, cocaine, hallucinogens, prescription drugs, and others on the human body, and insight into drug abuse prevention efforts employed in variety of settings.</p>

				<h4 id="PHE128" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHE 128 &nbsp; Disc Golf (1)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Disc Golf is a lifetime recreational game suitable for youth to senior citizens. It is played on disc golf courses using elevated baskets as holes, tee areas and various weight flying discs as drivers and putters. The structure of the game is the same as golf. The objective is to throw at each hole using the fewest attempts and is completed when the putt lands in the basket. The score is recorded and players move to the next tee to attempt the next hole. The player with the lowest score at the end of the course, wins the game.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

				<p>Pickleball is a lifetime recreational court game suitable for youth to senior citizens. It is played inside or out on a court using paddles, balls and a low net. The structure of the game court is the same size as a doubles badminton court.</p>

				<p>Introduction to diverse aspects of sports and sports studies. Study of how culture, values, society, and physical education/sport influence one another. Applied issues include legal, political, economic, cultural, and educational aspects of physical education and sport programs in schools and society.</p>

				<h4 id="PHE275" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHE 275 &nbsp; Psychological Aspects of Physical Education and Sport (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introduction to applied sport psychology, mental aspects of sports, and contemporary performance enhancement techniques. Includes theory and practice of sport psychology with mental aspects of training and competition, mental training techniques for psychomotor performance, and basic issues of performance psychology. Study of the following aspects of psychology as they influence performance: learning, practice, motivation, anxiety, perception, motor control, social facilitation, cohesion, retention, transfer, reinforcement, and leadership.</p>

					<h3>Physical Science</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PHY105" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 105 &nbsp; Environmental Geology (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Examination of geologic processes and hazards that influence human activities and the geologic aspects of pollution and waste-disposal.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																																<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHY107" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 107 &nbsp; Environmental Geology Laboratory (1)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> PHY 105-Environmental Geology.</p>
								
				<p>Exercises focus on environmental and social issues relevant to environmental problems and the effects of human interaction in geologic processes.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PHY111" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 111 &nbsp; Introduction to Physical Science (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introduces the basics in a variety of scientific disciplines including classical (Newtonian) physics, energy, matter and heat, wave behavior, electricity and magnetism, modern physics (the atom and nucleus), geology, and astronomy. Basic high school math/algebra is utilized in portions of this course.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																																<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHY113" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 113 &nbsp; Introduction to Physical Science Laboratory (1)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> Preceded or accompanied by PHY 111.</p>
								
				<p>Laboratory reinforces topics discussed in Physical Science lecture (PHY 111) by utilizing hands-on experimentation.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PHY125" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 125 &nbsp; Introduction to Physical Geology (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Introduces a basic understanding of topics in physical geology including the unifying theory of plate tectonics, discussions of Earth materials (rocks and minerals), internal processes (volcanism, earthquakes), surface processes (surface and ground water, weathering, erosion), and geologic time.&nbsp; Campus outings will be incorporated to emphasize Missouri geology.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																																<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHY127" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 127 &nbsp; Introduction to Physical Geology Laboratory (1)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> Preceded or accompanied by PHY 125.</p>
								
				<p>Laboratory reinforces topics discussed in Physical Geology lecture (PHY 125) by utilizing practical experimentation and observations.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>

				<h4 id="PHY130" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 130 &nbsp; Astronomy (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Nonmathematical introduction to astronomy designed primarily for non-science majors. Topics include the history and cultural impact of astronomy, properties of solar system, and stellar structures. Supplemented by occasional hours of evening observation.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>

				<h4 id="PHY131" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 131 &nbsp; Astronomy Laboratory (1)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> Preceded or accompanied by PHY 130 - Astronomy.</p>
								
				<p>Analysis and interpretation of astronomical data and observations with telescopes. No prior knowledge of astronomy assumed.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

																											</p>

				<h4 id="PHY145" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 145 &nbsp; Historical Geology (3)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> PHY 147</p>
								
				<p>Introduces an understanding of the history of Earth"s development including identification and interpretation of sediments, sedimentary rocks and rock structures, environments of deposition, major tectonic and depositional events of North America, and the evolution of life.&nbsp; Campus outings will be incorporated to emphasize Missouri geology.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PHY147" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 147 &nbsp; Historical Geology Laboratory (1)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> PHY 145</p>
								
				<p>Exercises in interpreting Earth's history by examination of sediments, sedimentary rocks, geologic time, and identification and taxonomic classification of fossils.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

				<h4 id="PHY150" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 150 &nbsp; General Physics I (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> MAT 150 or MAT 158 or MAT 162</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> PHY 153</p>
								
				<p>Survey of kinematics, dynamics, energy, momentum, rotational motion, fluids, and thermodynamics. Non-calculus in approach. Three hours of lecture-recitation and two hours of laboratory per week.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

																											</p>

				<h4 id="PHY151" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PHY 151 &nbsp; General Physics II (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PHY 150, PHY 153</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> PHY 154</p>
								
				<p>Begins with wave motion, but emphasis on electricity and magnetism. Treats geometric and wave optics. Non-calculus in approach. Three hours of lecture-recitation and two hours of laboratory per week.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

				<p>Experimental component of PHY 150.</p>

					<h3>Political Science</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="POL101" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 101 &nbsp; American Government (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Basic concepts of political science with major emphasis on origin, principles, organization, and nature of American federal system and its politics. POL 101 complies with provisions of Section 170.011 RsMo.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />

																																										<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="POL102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 102 &nbsp; State and Local Government (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Examines structure, functions, and operation of American state and local government within context of federalism. POL 102 complies with provisions of Section 170.011 RsMo.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="POL201" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 201 &nbsp; International Relations (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Any POL, HIS, or GEO.</p>
												
				<p>Study of factors shaping relationships among nations with emphasis upon developing nations and economic, political and environmental issues.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />

				<h4 id="POL210" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 210 &nbsp; Comparative Politics (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Any POL, HIS, or GEO.</p>
												
				<p>Analysis of ideologies, political cultures, and governmental structures of several different countries. Political systems of variety of nations chosen for study.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="POL220" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 220 &nbsp; Middle Eastern Politics (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Survey of Middle Eastern countries as well as regional issues and conflicts. Explores political development of the region, including discussions of Islam, nationalism, and international intervention.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="POL255" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 255 &nbsp; European Politics and Cultures (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Field course about European politics, history, and cultures in the context of a study tour. Explores the history of Europe and future of the European and future of the European Union through readings, films, writing assignments, and other activities. Among cultural issues, deals with the questions of what is ?Europe.? Specific course objectives outlined in learning agreement with the instructor.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="POL280" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">POL 280 &nbsp; Modern Britain (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>An introduction to the major aspects of political/social life in modern Britain: social stratification, the British political infrastructure, and dealing with published materials on British socio-political issues.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> POL 101 or POL 102, and instructor's permission.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> 2.5 GPA and sophomore standing.</p>

				<p>Exploration of one topic selected by department. Introduction to research techniques and seminar approved as integral part of scholarship.</p>

					<h3>Practical Nursing</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="NPN100" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 100 &nbsp; Personal and Vocational Concepts (1)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Acceptance into practical nursing program.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 101, NPN 111, NPN 121</p>
								
				<p>Role of LPN in relationship to other members of health care team is presented. Includes nursing history, professional ethics, and interpersonal relations in today's health care setting.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="NPN101" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 101 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Nursing (7)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Acceptance into practical nursing program.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 100, NPN 111, NPN 121, BIO 250A(240), BIO 250B(243), and ENG 096 or ENG 101.</p>
								
				<p>Emphasis is on the nursing process as students apply principles of physical, biological, and social sciences. Introduction of basic nutrition and pharmacology is included. Elements of health and disease and basic concepts of nursing are presented.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="NPN102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 102 &nbsp; Maternal-Child Nursing (6)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 250A(240), BIO 250B(243), ENG 096 or ENG 101, NPN 100, NPN 101, NPN 111, NPN 121.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 112</p>
								
				<p>Family centered approach to pregnancy, birth, and adaptation to extrauterine life is presented. Stressors involved in labor and delivery, human sexuality and its role in growth and development, diseases common to the pediatric client are explored. The impact of psychosocial, physical, and spiritual stressors, as well as common issues and problems encountered in individual, family, and community living are presented. Environmental and social health factors as related to appropriate developmental stages are discussed.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="NPN111" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 111 &nbsp; Fundamentals of Nursing Laboratory (0)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 100, NPN 101, NPN 121.</p>
								
				<p>Students gain comprehensive knowledge and ability to safely and accurately perform nursing skills in a safe learning environment using multi-media, textbooks, self-direction, demonstrations and faculty assistance. Skills included are: vital signs, hygiene and medical and surgical asepsis, partial ongoing assessment (shift assessment), mobility and medication administration.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

				<h4 id="NPN112" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 112 &nbsp; Maternal-Child Nursing Laboratory (0)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 102</p>
								
				<p>Students gain comprehensive knowledge and ability to safely and accurately perform nursing skills in a safe learning environment using multi-media, textbooks, self-direction, demonstrations and faculty assistance. Skills included are: sterile technique, dressing changes, urinary elimination, pediatric care and obstetrical care.</p>

													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 101, NPN 111.</p>
								
				<p>Students care for patients in nursing home, health care center, or hospital for a total of 80 clinical hours. Administration of medications is a part of clinical experience. Included in clinical hours is one hour for post conference for each day of clinical experience.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="NPN151" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 151 &nbsp; Medical Surgical Nursing I (11)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 250A(240), BIO 250B(243), ENG 096 or ENG 101, NPN 100, NPN 101, NPN 102, NPN 111, NPN 112, NPN 121.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 161, NPN 171, BIO 251A(241), BIO 251B(244), PSY 101.</p>
								
				<p>Emphasis on human growth and development while studying human adaptive and maladaptive responses to disturbances in nutrition and fluid balance, gastrointestinal, and other body systems. Presents illnesses that interfere with these processes throughout life span with focuses on physiological, psychological, psychosocial, and spiritual aspects during each stage of development.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="NPN152" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 152 &nbsp; Medical Surgical Nursing II (8)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> BIO 251A(241), BIO 251B(244), PSY 101, NPN 151, NPN 161, NPN 171.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 162, NPN 172.</p>
								
				<p>Continuation of study of adaptive and maladaptive responses to internal and external stressors that interfere with wellness and require nursing care. Includes beginning management as well as disturbances in endocrine, reproductive, and other body systems. Presents illnesses that interface with these processes throughout the life span with focus on physiological, psychological, psychosocial, and spiritual aspects during each stage of development.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

																											</p>

				<h4 id="NPN161" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">NPN 161 &nbsp; Medical Surgical Nursing I Laboratory (0)</h4>
				
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 151, NPN 171</p>
								
				<p>Students gain comprehensive knowledge and ability to safely and accurately perform nursing skills in a safe learning environment using multi-media, textbooks, self-direction, demonstrations and faculty assistance. Skills included are: peripheral intravenous therapy, nasogastric insertion, central venous catheters, enteral feedings and ostomy care.</p>

Observation experiences provided in operating room, recovery room, emergency room, and other hospital settings. Included in clinical hours is one post conference hour, for each day of clinical experience. A total of 182 clinical hours.</p>

													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> NPN 152, NPN 162</p>
								
				<p>Students learn beginning management skills to plan, administer, and evaluate nursing care to patients. Precepted hours in a health care facility are included. Clinical hours total are 112.</p>

					<h3>Psychology</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY101" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 101 &nbsp; Introduction to Psychology (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Examination of behavioral, cognitive, psychoanalytic, humanistic, and biological viewpoints in psychology. Includes learning principles and applications, perception, motivation, emotions, stress, psychobiology, personality, abnormal behavior, and approaches to therapy.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY201" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 201 &nbsp; Child Psychology (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Study of human development from conception to adolescence, emphasizing both current and historical approaches to research and theory, genetic and environmental influences on development, and sequence and timing of physical, mental, and personality development throughout years of childhood.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY210" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 210 &nbsp; Human Growth and Development (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Survey of basis of human growth and development. Review of emotional, mental, physical, and social needs of children, adolescents, and adults. Analysis of multiple factors that influence and shape behavior and personality.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY215" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 215 &nbsp; Adolescent Psychology (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Introduction to physical, mental, personality, and social developments unique to adolescence. Focus mainly on factors influencing normal development, but some abnormal behaviors discussed. Biological, psychological, cultural, and historical perspectives considered.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY216" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 216 &nbsp; Abnormal Psychology (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Survey of abnormal/deviant behavior, including causes and theories of anxiety disorders, psychoses, mental retardation, drug abuse, sexual disorders, criminal behavior, and other selected topics. Includes discussion of diagnosis, prevention, and treatment of these disorders.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY220" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 220 &nbsp; Personality Theories (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Study of major theories of personality with emphasis on developmental influence and integration of behavior. Theories surveyed represent dynamic, humanistic, cognitive, and behavioral perspectives. Issues such as self-concept, structure of personality, social adjustment, self-management, and maladjustment and therapy are considered within context of each theoretical system.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY225" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 225 &nbsp; Psychology of Aging (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Examination of psychological processes of aging involving sensory, sexual, intellectual, and personality changes in later life with some attention to common mental disorders in the aged.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY230" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 230 &nbsp; Social Psychology (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Study of social interaction of individuals and psychological principles and concepts involved in these relationships. Discussion of social perceptions, values, attitudes, prejudice, social influence, group dynamics, leadership, and other group processes.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY240" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 240 &nbsp; Introduction to Applied Behavior Analysis (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>This course is an introduction to applied behavior analysis and the application of behavioral principles and procedures to social challenges. The students will learn about the causes of behavior, basic principles and procedures, and then apply this information to specific content areas or populations.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY250" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 250 &nbsp; Drugs and Behavior (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>This course will address the many issues related to the use of psychoactive drugs. Students will learn about the biopsychological factors that underlie drug use and abuse while they examine specific individual drugs therapeutic psychoactive properties but also how long-term and/or excessive use modifies brain function. Students will learn how to distinguish between the science of psychopharmacology and the unsubstantiated claims of media, advertising and/or drug culture.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="PSY255" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 255 &nbsp; Brain and Behavior (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> PSY 101</p>
												
				<p>Examination of the human nervous system focusing on the central nervous system, the development and function of nerve cells and the relation between the brain and behavior. Topics include motivation, learning, sensation and perception, movement, emotions and brain dysfunction.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="PSY290" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">PSY 290 &nbsp; Special Topics in Psychology (1-3 hrs)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Selected studies in the field of psychology. Topics may include: psychological aspects of death, gender, issues in forensic psychology, diversity studies, preparation for marriage, child-rearing practices, and various other issues. Course may be repeated as topics vary by semester.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>

																											</p>
			</div>
				
					<h3>Reading</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="RDG080" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 080 &nbsp; Spelling I (2)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Individualized course of study presenting words with basic spelling patterns, complicated consonant patterns, and complicated vowel patterns. Word families and rules for addition of word endings included. Programmed learning techniques utilized.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="RDG081" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 081 &nbsp; Spelling II (2)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Individualized course of study presenting words with basic spelling patterns, complicated consonant patterns, and complicated vowel patterns. Word families and rules for addition of word endings included. Programmed learning techniques utilized.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="RDG083" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 083 &nbsp; Vocabulary Improvement (2)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Individualized course that provides programmed learning to guide through elements of vocabulary development. Includes directed practice in context clues, working with visually similar words and homonyms, and learning commonly misunderstood words.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="RDG084" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 084 &nbsp; Introduction to College Vocabulary (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Individualized, comprehensive course that provides programmed learning to guide through elements of college-level vocabulary. Includes Latin and Greek derivatives as well as words from fiction, drama, poetry, general literature, psychology, and foreign expressions. Emphasizes communication skills, and includes vocabulary as applied to rhetoric, figures of speech and clear, concise writing.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="RDG085" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 085 &nbsp; Reading Fundamentals (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> reading assessment test.</p>
												
				<p>This course is designed to help students expand the range of their reading comprehension and vocabulary skills with direct practice.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="RDG090" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 090 &nbsp; Vocabulary for College Reading (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Directed practice in college vocabulary skills emphasizing communication skills, figures of speech, rhetoric, and clear and concise writing. Course is ESL friendly.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="RDG092" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 092 &nbsp; Reading Improvement (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Course required based on assessment test reading scores or pass RDG085</p>
												
				<p>Directed practice in college reading skills; emphasizes word comprehension skills including context clues, dictionary use, and word components as well as paragraph comprehension skills including locating and inferring information.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="RDG093" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 093 &nbsp; Introduction to College Reading (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Course required based on assessment test reading scores or pass RDG 092.</p>
												
				<p>Provides directed practice in development of college reading skills, emphasizing vocabulary skills, comprehension skills, advanced reading skills, and reading for study. Vocabulary skills include dictionary use, word components and etymology, context clues, and multiple meanings of words. Comprehension skills include main ideas and support words signaling key concepts. Advanced reading skills include critical reading and reading efficiency. Reading for study includes effective textbook study methods, outlining, study mapping, summarizing, and textbook graphics.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="RDG104" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 104 &nbsp; Reading For Non-Native Speakers (4)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Accuplacer ESL Listening Test score of 67 to 79 plus placement with the oral interview as required by the Academic ESL Program Coordinator.</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> ESL 100, ESL 103 required  and a suggested corequisite of ESL 107.</p>
								
				<p>Directed practice in college reading skills emphasizing vocabulary, comprehension, critical thinking, reading efficiency and reading across the curriculum for non-native speaking students.&nbsp;</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="RDG106" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 106 &nbsp; Advanced Reading for Non-Native Speakers (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> ESL 103/SPE 100,and  ESL 104 with a minimum grade of C or better and ESL 100   </p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> ESL-105, and ESL-108 recommended</p>
								
				<p>Directed practice in advanced college reading skills emphasizing discipline specific vocabulary, advanced comprehension, higher level critical thinking skills, improved reading efficiency and reading across the curriculum for second-language students.&nbsp;</p>

				<h4 id="RDG111" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">RDG 111 &nbsp; Reading Across the Disciplines (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> ACT reading test score of 19 OR Accuplacer reading test score of 80 OR Nelson/Denny reading test score of 204 required.</p>
												
				<p>Focus is on improving reading and thinking skills through skill instruction and extensive guided-practice with academic discipline-based readings.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> Placement by ESL Chair or Reading Chair</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> ESL 101, ESL 102, unless waived by ESL or Reading Chair</p>
								
				<p>Focus will be on improving pronunciation and fluency, especially when reading aloud. Activities include spelling and phonics instruction as well as speaking and reading exercises designed to increase reader's fluency and natural voice when reading. A grade of "C" or better is needed to move into the next ESL class, ESL 104. Emphasis will be on speaking although writing will be part of the class curriculum as well.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">

					<h3>Sociology</h3>
	
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC101" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 101 &nbsp; Introduction to Sociology (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Examines relationship between individual and society in social structure of modern society. Introduction to way in which sociologists interpret and research human behavior. Covers patterns of social interaction and social influences on individual conduct.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/hybrid2.png" alt="Hybrid"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
															</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="SOC102" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 102 &nbsp; Introduction to Sociological Theory (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Examination of key figures in sociology. Introduction to history of sociology, sociologists, theoretical perspectives, and the classical and contemporary sociological theory and the application of theory to social groups, social interaction, and social institutions.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC151" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 151 &nbsp; Gerontology I (3)</h4>
				
												
				<p>Overview of normal effects of aging including physical, psychological, and social changes. Problems associated with aging, such as increased dependence, loss of health, financial constraints, loss of friends and spouse, and altered living arrangements. Content presented from perspective of aging person and society as a whole.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="SOC201" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 201 &nbsp; Contemporary Social Issues (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101</p>
												
				<p>Study of major social problems facing human groups in modern society such as deviance, inequality, war, and overpopulation. Emphasis placed on social problems that arise as result of institutional fluctuations in economy, family, government, religion, science, and technology.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC210" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 210 &nbsp; Sociology of Health and Healthcare (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101 or equivalent</p>
												
				<p>Examination of the social, economic, cultural and individual factors in age related health issues. Topics include epidemiology, social structuring of age, healthcare services, policies and programs, as well as relationships between doctors and patients.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="SOC215" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 215 &nbsp; Marriage and the Family (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101</p>
												
				<p>Reviews historical development of the family and patterns of intimate relationships in modern society. Analysis of institution of family in terms of relationship to other institutions in society. Specific topics include love, dating, parenting, families in crisis, and alternative lifestyles.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																																										<img src="/images/icons/online2.png" alt="Online"  style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																					</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC221" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 221 &nbsp; Sociology of Art (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101, ENG 101</p>
													<p><strong>Corequisites:</strong> Suggested corequisite: ART 101 or ART 150.</p>
								
				<p>Major trends in art examined in relationship to socio-historical developments. Art seen as both comment on and reflection of society. Team taught by sociology instructor and art instructor.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="SOC224" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 224 &nbsp; Sex, Gender, and Society (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101</p>
												
				<p>Focus on analysis of women and men in society and culture. Multiple disciplines examined as means to study social processes through which sex roles develop and are acquired. Examines individual and social consequences of sex differences and sex inequality.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC241" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 241 &nbsp; Sociology Through Literature (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101, ENG 101</p>
												
				<p>Application of sociological concepts to literature to analyze literature as social commentary. Variety of literary selections used to analyze socio-historical events and movements.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em;  background: #f0f0f0 ">
				<h4 id="SOC251" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 251 &nbsp; Aspects of Aging (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101</p>
												
				<p>Focus on social variables and forces that affect the aging process. Topics include sociological theories of aging, technological and social change and effects on environment of older people, and prejudice and discrimination against elderly.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
																		<img src="/images/icons/on-campus2.png" alt="On-Campus" style="margin-right: .75rem; vertical-align: middle;" />
																											</p>
			</div>
					<div style="padding: 0 1em; ">
				<h4 id="SOC290" style="margin-top: 0; padding-top: 1em;">SOC 290 &nbsp; Readings in Sociology (3)</h4>
				
									<p><strong>Prerequisites:</strong> SOC 101, ENG 101</p>
												
				<p>Focus on specific social phenomenon. Topic varies depending on semester and instructor. Students encouraged to suggest topics of interest.</p>
				
				<p style="margin-top: -10px;">
					<span style="margin-right: .5rem; vertical-align: super;">Course Type(s):</span>
